### Subsection: 9.4a Problem Statement

In this section, we will discuss the problem of pollution mitigation and externalities in the context of urban development. As cities continue to grow and expand, the issue of pollution and externalities becomes increasingly important. Pollution refers to the release of harmful substances into the environment, while externalities are costs or benefits that are not reflected in the market price of a good or service.

#### The Problem of Pollution Mitigation and Externalities

The problem of pollution mitigation and externalities arises when the costs of pollution are not fully reflected in the market price of a good or service. This can lead to overproduction and overconsumption, resulting in negative externalities such as environmental degradation and health impacts. In the context of urban development, this can have significant implications for the well-being of residents and the overall sustainability of the city.

One example of this is the issue of air pollution in cities. As more cars are driven and more factories operate, the amount of pollutants in the air increases. This can have negative impacts on the health of residents, particularly those with respiratory issues. However, the cost of this pollution is not fully reflected in the market price of gasoline or the products produced by these factories. This leads to overconsumption and further pollution.

#### Solutions to the Problem

To address the problem of pollution mitigation and externalities, economists have proposed various solutions. One solution is to implement a carbon tax, which would place a price on the emission of carbon dioxide and other greenhouse gases. This would encourage individuals and businesses to reduce their carbon footprint and invest in cleaner technologies.

Another solution is to implement a cap-and-trade system, where a limit is set on the total amount of emissions allowed and companies can buy and sell emission permits. This would create an incentive for companies to reduce their emissions in order to save on the cost of permits.

In addition to these market-based solutions, there are also regulatory solutions that can be implemented. For example, stricter emission standards can be put in place for vehicles and factories, requiring them to reduce their pollution levels. This can be accompanied by enforcement measures to ensure compliance.

#### Conclusion

The problem of pollution mitigation and externalities is a complex and pressing issue in the context of urban development. It requires a multifaceted approach that combines market-based solutions, regulatory measures, and public education. By addressing this problem, we can work towards creating more sustainable and livable cities for future generations.





### Subsection: 9.4b Solution Approach

In this section, we will discuss the approach to solving the problem of pollution mitigation and externalities. As mentioned in the previous section, there are various solutions that have been proposed by economists. However, it is important to consider the effectiveness and feasibility of these solutions in the context of urban development.

#### The Role of Economic Analysis

Economic analysis plays a crucial role in understanding and addressing the problem of pollution mitigation and externalities. By using economic models and tools, we can quantify the costs and benefits of different solutions and evaluate their effectiveness. This allows us to make informed decisions and develop policies that can mitigate pollution and externalities.

One approach to economic analysis is the use of market-based instruments, such as carbon taxes and cap-and-trade systems. These instruments aim to internalize the externalities of pollution by placing a price on it. By doing so, they create an incentive for individuals and businesses to reduce their pollution levels and invest in cleaner technologies.

Another approach is the use of command-and-control regulations, which set specific emission standards and require companies to meet them. These regulations can be effective in reducing pollution, but they can also be costly and may not address all externalities.

#### The Importance of Collaboration and Cooperation

In addition to economic analysis, collaboration and cooperation among different stakeholders is crucial in addressing the problem of pollution mitigation and externalities. This includes government agencies, businesses, and the community. By working together, we can develop more comprehensive and effective solutions that consider the needs and concerns of all stakeholders.

For example, in the context of urban development, collaboration between government agencies and businesses can lead to the implementation of green building codes and incentives for sustainable practices. This not only reduces pollution, but also creates jobs and stimulates the economy. Collaboration with the community can also lead to the development of community-based initiatives, such as recycling programs and public transportation systems, which can further mitigate pollution and externalities.

#### The Role of Education and Awareness

Finally, education and awareness play a crucial role in addressing the problem of pollution mitigation and externalities. By educating individuals and businesses about the impacts of pollution and the benefits of sustainable practices, we can create a culture of environmental responsibility. This can lead to changes in behavior and attitudes that can have a significant impact on pollution levels.

In addition, raising awareness through media and public outreach can also help to create a sense of urgency and motivate individuals and businesses to take action. By working together, we can create a more sustainable and livable urban environment for all.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored various solutions to the complex problems faced by planners and policymakers. We have discussed the importance of using economic analysis and decision-making tools to address these issues and have provided a comprehensive guide to help readers understand and apply these concepts.

We began by discussing the role of economic analysis in policy-making and how it can help us understand the potential impacts of different policies. We then delved into the different types of economic models and techniques that can be used to analyze and evaluate policies, such as cost-benefit analysis, cost-effectiveness analysis, and game theory. We also explored the concept of externalities and how they can affect the outcomes of policies.

Next, we discussed the importance of considering equity and distributional effects in policy-making. We explored the concept of distributive justice and how it can be used to evaluate the fairness of policies. We also discussed the role of redistributive policies in addressing income inequality.

Finally, we discussed the importance of considering the long-term effects of policies and the need for sustainable solutions. We explored the concept of intergenerational equity and how it can be used to evaluate the impacts of policies on future generations. We also discussed the role of discounting and how it can affect our decision-making processes.

Overall, this chapter has provided readers with a comprehensive guide to public policy analysis and decision-making. By understanding the economic concepts and tools discussed, readers will be better equipped to address the complex problems faced by planners and policymakers.

Exams are not just about testing one's knowledge; they are also about learning. The process of preparing for an exam can be a valuable learning experience, as it forces one to engage with the material in a more profound way. This chapter will explore this aspect of exams, providing you with strategies and techniques to make the most out of your exam preparation.

Finally, we will discuss the role of exams in the overall academic journey. Exams are not just a means to an end; they are an integral part of the learning process. They provide a structured way to assess one's progress and identify areas of improvement. This chapter will help you understand the significance of exams in your academic journey and how to approach them with confidence and clarity.

As we delve into the world of exams, remember that they are not just about testing your knowledge, but also about learning and growing. They are a crucial part of the academic journey, and this chapter aims to provide you with a comprehensive guide to navigating this aspect of planning economics.




### Section: 10.1 Final Exam:

The final exam for "Planning Economics: A Comprehensive Guide to Public Policy Analysis and Decision Making" is designed to assess your understanding of the key concepts and principles covered in the book. It is a comprehensive exam that tests your knowledge, critical thinking, and problem-solving skills. The exam is divided into three parts, each covering a different aspect of planning economics.

#### 10.1a Exam Format

The final exam is a written exam, which you will take on a computer. The exam is divided into three parts, each covering a different aspect of planning economics. The exam is designed to be completed in three hours.

1. Part A: Multiple-Choice Questions (1 hour â 30% of total marks)

Part A consists of 50 multiple-choice questions. Each question carries one mark. The questions are designed to test your knowledge of the key concepts and principles covered in the book. The questions may be based on the reading passages, lecture notes, or practice problems.

2. Part B: Short Answer Questions (1 hour â 30% of total marks)

Part B consists of 10 short answer questions. Each question carries two marks. The questions are designed to test your understanding of the key concepts and principles covered in the book. The questions may be based on the reading passages, lecture notes, or practice problems.

3. Part C: Essay Questions (1 hour â 40% of total marks)

Part C consists of three essay questions. Each essay carries four marks. The questions are designed to test your critical thinking and problem-solving skills. The questions may be based on the reading passages, lecture notes, or practice problems.

The final exam is a comprehensive assessment of your understanding of planning economics. It is designed to test your knowledge, critical thinking, and problem-solving skills. The exam is a crucial component of your learning journey, and it is essential to prepare for it thoroughly.

In the next section, we will discuss some strategies and techniques to help you prepare for the final exam.

#### 10.1b Exam Review

After completing the final exam, it is crucial to take some time to review your performance. This review process will help you identify areas of strength and weakness, and guide your future study and work in planning economics.

1. Review Your Answers: Start by reviewing your answers to the multiple-choice questions in Part A. If you answered a question incorrectly, try to understand why you made that mistake. Was it because you didn't understand the concept, or because you misread the question? Make note of these mistakes and work on improving your understanding of these concepts.

2. Reflect on Your Short Answers: Next, review your short answers in Part B. Consider whether your answers were clear and concise. Did you fully address the question? If not, try to understand why. Perhaps you didn't fully understand the question, or you didn't have enough information to answer it. Make note of these areas for improvement.

3. Analyze Your Essays: Finally, review your essays in Part C. Consider the structure of your essays, the clarity of your arguments, and the depth of your analysis. Did you fully answer the question? If not, try to understand why. Perhaps you didn't fully understand the question, or you didn't have enough information to answer it. Make note of these areas for improvement.

4. Seek Feedback: Don't hesitate to seek feedback from your instructors. They can provide valuable insights into your performance and help guide your future study and work in planning economics.

5. Plan for Improvement: Based on your review and feedback, make a plan for improvement. What concepts do you need to work on? What study strategies will help you improve? What changes will you make in your approach to planning economics?

Remember, the final exam is just one part of your learning journey in planning economics. It is a valuable opportunity to assess your understanding and guide your future study and work. By taking the time to review your performance and plan for improvement, you can make the most of this opportunity and continue to grow in your understanding of planning economics.

#### 10.1c Exam Tips

As you prepare for your final exam in planning economics, here are some tips to help you perform your best:

1. Practice, Practice, Practice: The best way to prepare for any exam is to practice. Use the practice problems provided in the book, and seek out additional practice materials. The more you practice, the more familiar you will become with the types of questions that may be asked, and the better prepared you will be.

2. Understand the Format: Make sure you understand the format of the exam. How many sections are there? How long is each section? What types of questions are asked in each section? Understanding the format can help you manage your time effectively during the exam.

3. Review Your Notes: Review your lecture notes and reading notes. Make sure you understand the key concepts and principles covered in the course. If there are any areas you are unsure about, seek clarification from your instructors.

4. Prepare a Study Guide: Creating a study guide can be a helpful way to review and organize your notes. A study guide can help you identify areas of strength and weakness, and guide your future study and work in planning economics.

5. Get a Good Night's Sleep: Make sure you get a good night's sleep before the exam. A good night's sleep can help you stay focused and perform your best on the exam.

6. Stay Calm and Focused: During the exam, stay calm and focused. Take your time with each question. If you get stuck on a question, move on and come back to it later if time allows.

7. Show Your Work: Even if you can't find the final answer, showing your work can earn you partial credit. Make sure you fully answer each question, even if you can't find the final answer.

8. Review Your Answers: After completing the exam, take some time to review your answers. If you have time, try to answer any questions you skipped. Even if you can't answer them, reviewing your answers can help you understand the exam better.

Remember, the final exam is just one part of your learning journey in planning economics. It is a valuable opportunity to assess your understanding and guide your future study and work in planning economics. Good luck!

### Subsection: 10.1c Exam Preparation

Preparing for the final exam of Planning Economics: A Comprehensive Guide to Public Policy Analysis and Decision Making is crucial for success in this course. The exam covers all the material from the textbook, so it is important to review and understand all the concepts and theories discussed in each chapter.

#### Tips for Exam Preparation

1. Review your notes: Take the time to review your notes from each chapter. This will help you identify any areas that you may need to focus on more during your studying.

2. Practice with sample questions: The textbook provides sample questions for each chapter. These questions are a great way to test your understanding and identify any areas that you may need to work on.

3. Understand the format of the exam: The final exam is divided into three parts, covering all four language skills (Reading, Writing, Listening, and Speaking). Make sure you understand the format of the exam and how much time is allotted for each section.

4. Prepare for the Reading and Writing paper: This paper has eight parts and 42 questions. Make sure you are familiar with the types of texts and tasks that may be included on the exam. Practice reading and answering questions based on different types of texts, such as signs, brochures, and emails.

5. Prepare for the Listening paper: This paper has four parts and 25 questions. Make sure you are familiar with the types of listening tasks that may be included on the exam. Practice listening to a variety of spoken materials and answering questions based on what you hear.

6. Prepare for the Speaking paper: This paper is taken face-to-face and candidates have the choice of taking the Reading and Writing paper and Listening paper on either a computer or on paper. Make sure you are comfortable with both formats and are able to effectively communicate your ideas and understanding.

By following these tips and practicing with sample questions, you can feel more confident and prepared for the final exam. Good luck!

### Subsection: 10.2a Problem Statement

In this section, we will be discussing the problem statement for the economic structure of cities. This problem statement is a crucial aspect of understanding the economic dynamics of cities and how they can be analyzed and improved.

#### The Economic Structure of Cities

The economic structure of a city refers to the composition of its economy, including the industries and businesses that operate within its boundaries. It also includes the relationships between these industries and businesses, as well as their interactions with the local government and community.

#### The Importance of Understanding the Economic Structure of Cities

Understanding the economic structure of a city is essential for policymakers, planners, and businesses. It allows them to identify the strengths and weaknesses of the economy, as well as potential areas for growth and improvement. By understanding the economic structure, they can make informed decisions and policies that can have a positive impact on the city's economy.

#### The Problem Statement

The problem statement for the economic structure of cities is a comprehensive analysis of the city's economy, including its industries, businesses, and relationships. It involves identifying the key factors that influence the city's economy, such as demographics, infrastructure, and government policies. It also includes examining the interactions between these factors and how they contribute to the overall economic structure of the city.

#### The Role of Public Policy Analysis and Decision Making

Public policy analysis and decision making play a crucial role in understanding and improving the economic structure of cities. By using economic models and data, policymakers and planners can analyze the impact of different policies and decisions on the city's economy. This allows them to make informed decisions that can have a positive impact on the city's economic growth and development.

## Chapter 11: Exams:




### Introduction

By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the purpose and importance of exams, as well as the necessary skills and strategies to excel in them. ### Conclusion

We have discussed the importance of exams in evaluating the effectiveness of public policies and how they can be used to inform future policy decisions. We have also examined the different types of exams, such as multiple-choice, short answer, and essay exams, and how they can be used to assess different levels of knowledge and understanding.

Exams are an essential tool in the field of planning economics, as they allow us to assess the impact of public policies on a large scale. By testing a representative sample of the population, we can gather valuable data on the effectiveness of policies and make informed decisions for the future. Exams also provide a means of evaluating the performance of different policy options, allowing us to identify the most effective solutions.

However, exams also have their limitations. They may not accurately reflect the real-world application of policies, and they can be influenced by factors such as test-taking skills and test anxiety. Therefore, it is crucial to use exams in conjunction with other methods, such as surveys and interviews, to gain a comprehensive understanding of policy effectiveness.

In conclusion, exams play a crucial role in public policy analysis and decision making. They provide a means of evaluating the impact of policies and informing future decisions. However, they should be used in conjunction with other methods to gain a more comprehensive understanding of policy effectiveness.

Finally, we will explore the role of exams in decision-making processes in planning economics. Exams are used to evaluate the effectiveness of economic policies and decisions, and they play a crucial role in informing future policy decisions. We will discuss how exams can be used to assess the impact of economic policies and identify areas for improvement.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide to exams in the field of planning economics. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the different types of exams, their format and structure, and their importance in economic education and decision-making processes. 


## Chapter 11: Exams:




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the various aspects of public policy analysis and decision making through the lens of exams. We have discussed the importance of exams in evaluating the effectiveness of public policies and how they can be used to inform future policy decisions. We have also examined the different types of exams, such as multiple-choice, short answer, and essay exams, and how they can be used to assess different levels of knowledge and understanding.

Exams are an essential tool in the field of planning economics, as they allow us to assess the impact of public policies on a large scale. By testing a representative sample of the population, we can gather valuable data on the effectiveness of policies and make informed decisions for the future. Exams also provide a means of evaluating the performance of different policy options, allowing us to identify the most effective solutions.

However, exams also have their limitations. They may not accurately reflect the real-world application of policies, and they can be influenced by factors such as test-taking skills and test anxiety. Therefore, it is crucial to use exams in conjunction with other methods, such as surveys and interviews, to gain a comprehensive understanding of policy effectiveness.

In conclusion, exams play a crucial role in public policy analysis and decision making. They provide a means of evaluating the impact of policies and informing future decisions. However, they should be used in conjunction with other methods to gain a more comprehensive understanding of policy effectiveness.

## Chapter 11: Exams:




### Introduction

Welcome to Chapter 11 of "Planning Economics: A Comprehensive Guide to Public Policy Analysis and Decision Making". This chapter serves as a syllabus for the book, providing an overview of the topics covered and the key concepts that will be explored.

In this book, we aim to provide a comprehensive understanding of planning economics, with a focus on public policy analysis and decision making. We will delve into the complexities of economic planning, exploring the various factors that influence economic decisions and the methods used to analyze and evaluate these decisions.

The book is structured to provide a logical progression of topics, starting with an introduction to economic planning and its importance in public policy. We will then explore the various tools and techniques used in economic analysis, including cost-benefit analysis, cost-effectiveness analysis, and cost-utility analysis. We will also discuss the role of economic models in policy analysis, including the use of general equilibrium models and partial equilibrium models.

As we progress through the book, we will also examine the role of economic planning in different sectors, including transportation, energy, and healthcare. We will discuss the challenges and opportunities in these sectors, and how economic planning can be used to address these issues.

Throughout the book, we will also explore the ethical considerations in economic planning, including the role of equity and fairness in decision making. We will also discuss the role of stakeholders and the importance of public participation in economic planning.

By the end of this book, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of planning economics and its role in public policy. They will also have the tools and knowledge to critically analyze and evaluate economic decisions, and to participate in the planning process.

We hope that this book will serve as a valuable resource for students, researchers, and policymakers interested in understanding and improving economic planning. Thank you for joining us on this journey through the world of planning economics.




### Section: 11.1 Course Overview:

Welcome to the first section of Chapter 11, where we will provide an overview of the course. This section will serve as a guide for the rest of the book, providing a roadmap for the topics covered and the key concepts that will be explored.

#### 11.1a Course Description

"Planning Economics: A Comprehensive Guide to Public Policy Analysis and Decision Making" is a book designed to provide a comprehensive understanding of planning economics, with a focus on public policy analysis and decision making. The book is structured to provide a logical progression of topics, starting with an introduction to economic planning and its importance in public policy.

The book will then delve into the various tools and techniques used in economic analysis, including cost-benefit analysis, cost-effectiveness analysis, and cost-utility analysis. We will also discuss the role of economic models in policy analysis, including the use of general equilibrium models and partial equilibrium models.

As we progress through the book, we will also examine the role of economic planning in different sectors, including transportation, energy, and healthcare. We will discuss the challenges and opportunities in these sectors, and how economic planning can be used to address these issues.

Throughout the book, we will also explore the ethical considerations in economic planning, including the role of equity and fairness in decision making. We will also discuss the role of stakeholders and the importance of public participation in economic planning.

By the end of this book, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of planning economics and its role in public policy. They will also have the tools and knowledge to critically analyze and evaluate economic decisions, and to participate in the planning process.

#### 11.1b Course Objectives

The primary objective of this course is to provide students with a comprehensive understanding of planning economics and its role in public policy analysis and decision making. By the end of this course, students should be able to:

1. Understand the basic principles of economic planning and its importance in public policy.
2. Apply cost-benefit analysis, cost-effectiveness analysis, and cost-utility analysis to evaluate economic decisions.
3. Use economic models, such as general equilibrium models and partial equilibrium models, to analyze policy decisions.
4. Analyze the role of economic planning in different sectors, including transportation, energy, and healthcare.
5. Understand the ethical considerations in economic planning, including the role of equity and fairness in decision making.
6. Understand the role of stakeholders and the importance of public participation in economic planning.
7. Critically analyze and evaluate economic decisions, and participate in the planning process.

#### 11.1c Course Outline

The course is divided into several modules, each covering a specific topic in planning economics. The modules are as follows:

1. Introduction to Economic Planning and Public Policy: This module will provide an overview of economic planning and its importance in public policy. It will also introduce the basic concepts and principles of economic planning.
2. Economic Analysis Tools: This module will delve into the various tools and techniques used in economic analysis, including cost-benefit analysis, cost-effectiveness analysis, and cost-utility analysis.
3. Economic Models in Policy Analysis: This module will discuss the role of economic models in policy analysis, including the use of general equilibrium models and partial equilibrium models.
4. Economic Planning in Different Sectors: This module will examine the role of economic planning in different sectors, including transportation, energy, and healthcare.
5. Ethical Considerations in Economic Planning: This module will explore the ethical considerations in economic planning, including the role of equity and fairness in decision making.
6. Stakeholder Analysis and Public Participation: This module will discuss the role of stakeholders and the importance of public participation in economic planning.
7. Critical Analysis and Evaluation of Economic Decisions: This module will provide students with the tools and knowledge to critically analyze and evaluate economic decisions.

Each module will be accompanied by readings, lectures, and assignments to help students understand the concepts and apply them in real-world scenarios. By the end of this course, students will have a comprehensive understanding of planning economics and its role in public policy analysis and decision making.

#### 11.2 Course Schedule:

The course schedule for Planning Economics: A Comprehensive Guide to Public Policy Analysis and Decision Making is designed to provide students with a comprehensive understanding of the subject matter while also allowing for ample time for independent study and application of concepts. The course is divided into three main components: lectures, readings, and assignments.

##### 11.2a Weekly Schedule

The weekly schedule for this course is as follows:

1. **Lectures**: There will be two lectures per week, each lasting 90 minutes. These lectures will cover the key concepts and theories of planning economics, as well as their practical applications in public policy analysis and decision making.

2. **Readings**: Students are expected to complete assigned readings before each lecture. These readings will be drawn from a variety of sources, including textbooks, academic articles, and real-world case studies.

3. **Assignments**: There will be regular assignments throughout the course, including quizzes, problem sets, and case studies. These assignments will help students apply the concepts learned in lectures and readings to real-world scenarios.

4. **Office Hours**: The instructor will hold weekly office hours for students to ask questions and discuss course material. These sessions will be held in [location] at [time].

5. **Exams**: There will be two exams throughout the course, a mid-term and a final. These exams will test students' understanding of the course material and their ability to apply it to real-world scenarios.

6. **Final Project**: The final project will be a culmination of all the concepts learned throughout the course. Students will be required to apply these concepts to a real-world economic planning problem and present their findings to the class.

By following this schedule and completing all assignments, students will gain a comprehensive understanding of planning economics and be able to apply this knowledge to real-world scenarios.

##### 11.2b Grading Policy

The grading policy for this course is as follows:

1. **Assignments (40%)**: Assignments will be graded based on their completeness and accuracy. Late assignments will be accepted up to 24 hours after the due date with a 10% penalty.

2. **Exams (40%)**: Exams will be graded based on their completeness and accuracy. The mid-term exam will count for 20% of the final grade, and the final exam will count for 20%.

3. **Final Project (20%)**: The final project will be graded based on its complexity, analysis, and presentation.

4. **Participation (10%)**: Participation in class discussions and office hours will be graded based on engagement and contribution.

By following this grading policy, students will be able to track their progress throughout the course and understand their final grade. Any questions or concerns about the grading policy should be directed to the instructor.

#### 11.2b Important Dates

In addition to the weekly schedule, there are several important dates to keep in mind throughout the course. These dates are crucial for students to stay on track and complete all necessary assignments and exams.

1. **First Day of Class**: The first day of class will be [date] and will be used to introduce the course and its expectations. Students are expected to attend this class and bring their textbooks.

2. **Mid-Term Exam**: The mid-term exam will be held on [date] and will cover all material taught in the first half of the course. Students are expected to prepare for this exam by completing all assigned readings and assignments.

3. **Final Exam**: The final exam will be held on [date] and will cover all material taught in the course. Students are expected to prepare for this exam by completing all assigned readings and assignments, as well as reviewing their notes and assignments from throughout the course.

4. **Final Project Due Date**: The final project is due on [date] and must be submitted by the end of the day. Students are expected to work on this project throughout the course and seek help from the instructor if needed.

5. **Last Day of Class**: The last day of class will be [date] and will be used to review course material and prepare for the final exam. Students are expected to attend this class and bring any remaining assignments or questions.

By following this schedule and completing all assignments and exams, students will gain a comprehensive understanding of planning economics and be able to apply this knowledge to real-world scenarios. It is important for students to manage their time effectively and seek help from the instructor if needed. Good luck!





#### 11.2c Exam Schedule

In addition to the weekly schedule, there are several important dates to keep in mind throughout the course. These dates are crucial for students to stay on track and complete all necessary assignments and exams.

3. **Final Exam**: The final exam will be held on [date] and will cover all material taught in the course. Students are expected to prepare for this exam by completing all assigned readings and assignments, as well as reviewing their notes and assignments from throughout the course.

4. **Final Project Due Date**: The final project is due on [date] and must be submitted by the end of the day. Students are expected to work on this project throughout the course and seek help from the instructor if needed.

5. **Last Day of Class**: The last day of class will be [date] and will be used to review course material and prepare for the final exam. Students are expected to attend this class and bring any remaining assignments or questions.

By following this schedule and completing all assignments and exams, students will gain a comprehensive understanding of planning economics and be able to apply this knowledge to real-world scenarios. It is important for students to manage their time effectively and seek help from the instructor if needed. Good luck!





#### 11.3a Attendance Policy

Attendance is an important aspect of this course and is crucial for students to fully understand and apply the concepts taught in planning economics. As such, students are expected to attend all classes and arrive on time. If a student is unable to attend a class due to illness or other extenuating circumstances, they must inform the instructor as soon as possible. Repeated absences without a valid excuse will result in a lower grade or even a failing grade.

#### 11.3b Grading Policy

The final grade for this course will be based on a combination of assignments, exams, and class participation. Assignments will make up 30% of the grade, exams will make up 60%, and class participation will make up 10%. The remaining 10% will be based on the completion of a final project, which will be due at the end of the course.

#### 11.3c Academic Integrity

Academic integrity is a fundamental principle in academia that emphasizes the importance of honesty, trust, fairness, and responsibility in all academic activities. It is the responsibility of each student to uphold academic integrity in all aspects of their work, including assignments, exams, and research.

Plagiarism, cheating, and other forms of academic dishonesty are strictly prohibited and will not be tolerated in this course. Any act of academic dishonesty will result in severe consequences, including a failing grade for the course. It is important for students to properly cite all sources used in their work and to avoid any form of cheating or plagiarism.

#### 11.3d Accommodations for Students with Disabilities

Students with disabilities may request accommodations for this course. It is the student's responsibility to provide documentation of their disability and discuss accommodations with the instructor. Accommodations will be made to the extent possible without fundamentally altering the nature of the course.

#### 11.3e Communication

Students are encouraged to communicate with the instructor if they have any questions or concerns about the course. The instructor will respond to emails within 24 hours, except on weekends and holidays. Students are also encouraged to discuss course material and assignments with their classmates and seek help from the instructor if needed.

At the end of the course, students will have the opportunity to evaluate the course and provide feedback on their learning experience. It is the student's responsibility to provide documentation of the circumstances and discuss accommodations with the instructor. Accommodations will be made to the extent possible without fundamentally altering the nature of the course.
